Jamison Brereton

54 (408)
Maruts
┼Ъy─Бv─Б┼Ыva ─Аtreya
15 verses: jagat─л, except triс╣гс╣нubh 14
One of the most intensely descriptive of the Marut hymns, with shifting images of the violent thunderstorms and welcome rain that they provoke. There is no particular progress or development in the hymn, just the succession of exuberant descriptions. The last three verses (13тАУ15) shift to prayers for the MarutsтАЩ gifts and help.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Maruts

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOffer praise to the company of the Maruts, the self-irradiating, the precipitators of mountains; present liberal oblations to the assuagers of heat, to those who come from the sky, to whom solemn rites are familiar, to the givers of abundant food.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

To whom solemn rites are familiar: pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нhayajvane: by whom the sacrifices called pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нha are made, these are said to be six, of which two are specified: rathantara and bс╣Ыhat, ┼Ыatpс╣Ыс╣гс╣нhaiс╕е rathantara bс╣Ыhad─Бdibhir ij─Бn─Бya

Jamison Brereton

ForthтАФfor the Marut troop with its own radiance I will anoint this speech, for (the troop) shaking the mountains,
for (the troop) with the rhythm of the gharma pot, sacrificing on the back of heaven, of heaven-bright fameтАФsing (forth) their great
manliness.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first word of the hymn is pr├б, as it was in V.52, the first of ┼Ъy─Бv─Б┼ЫvaтАЩs Marut hymns. It would at first appear to be in tmesis with anaj─Б in b (so Grassmann and see RenouтАЩs bizarre tr. тАЬje veux lancer-avec-onctionтАЭ), but тИЪa├▒j does not otherwise appear with pr├б. I think it rather belongs with the last word of the vs., arcata. The syntagm pr├б тИЪarc is quite common and, more to the point, began the first hymn in this cycle: V.52.1ab pr├б тАж, ├бrc─Б. The rest of our vs., from ┼Ы├бrdh─Бya to dyumn├б┼Ыravase, is set into this celebratory frame.

anaj─Б is the 1st sg. act. nasal infix pres. subjunctive, as all the standard tr. take it, pace its assignment to the pf. by Grassmann, Wh, Macdonell

My tr. of gharmast├║bh- тАШwith the rhythm of the gharma-potтАЩ sounds like a bahuvr─лhi, which it is not. Better would be тАШchanting rhymically (like) the gharmapotтАЩ (cf. chandast├║bh- in nearby V.52.12). The point of comparison, as is noted by most comm., is the regular bubbling of the gharma-pot.

My тАЬsacrificing on the back of heavenтАЭ agrees with Geldner and Renou in taking div├бс╕е as limiting the first member of pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нhay├бjvane. Oldenberg allows both this and a syntagm div├б ─Б╠БтАЬfrom heaven,тАЭ while Witzel Got┼Н follow OldenbergтАЩs 2nd alternative and suggest that the Maruts are sacrificing on the back of the earth (to be supplied). It is difficult to make a judgment here.

Griffith

THIS hymn will I make for the Marut host who bright in native splendour cast the mountains down.
Sing the great strength of those illustrious in renown, who stay the heat, who sacrifice on heights of heaven.

Geldner

Der marutischen Heerschar, der selbstgl├дnzenden, Berge ersch├╝tternden, will ich diese Rede als Schmuck anlegen; die wie der hei├Яe Milchtrank singt, die auf des Himmels R├╝cken opfert, der glanzber├╝hmten preiset ihren hohen Mannesmut!

Grassmann

Der Marutschar habt kunstvoll ihr dies Lied erdacht, die gl├дnzend strahlt und die die Berge beben macht; Der kraftber├╝hmten singt ein grosses Heldenlied, die blitzend rauscht und herstr├╢mt von des Himmels H├╢h.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрдм рдкрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╣ рдЛрдЪрд╛рд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдЪреМрд╡рдирд╡реЗрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд░рдореНрдн рд╣реИ, рдЙрд╕рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рдердо рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдХреИрд╕реЗ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ, рдЗрд╕ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рджрд┐рд╡рдГ) рдХрд╛рдордирд╛ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛ ! рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧ (рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рдирд╡реЗ) рдЕрдкрдиреА рдХрд╛рдиреНрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рди рдЬрд┐рд╕рдХреЗ рдЙрд╕ (рдорд╛рд░реБрддрд╛рдп) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзреА (рд╢рд░реНрдзрд╛рдп) рдмрд▓ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдЗрдорд╛рдореН) рдЗрд╕ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди (рд╡рд╛рдЪрдореН) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдд рд╡рд╛рдгреА рдХрд╛ (рдкреНрд░рд╛рдирдЬ) рдЙрдЪреНрдЪрд╛рд░рдг рдХреАрдЬрд┐рдпреЗ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рджреАрдЬрд┐рдпреЗ рдФрд░ (рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрдЪреНрдпреБрддреЗ) рдореЗрдШ рд╕реЗ рдЧрд┐рд░реЗ рд╡рд╛ рдЬреЛ рдореЗрдШ рдХреЛ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд╛рддрд╛ (рдШрд░реНрдорд╕реНрддреБрднреЗ) рдпрдЬреНрдЮ рдХреА рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рдФрд░ (рдкреГрд╖реНрдардпрдЬреНрд╡рдиреЗ) рдкреГрд╖реНрда рд╕реЗ рдпрдЬреНрдЮ рдХрд░рддрд╛ (рджреНрдпреБрдореНрдирд╢реНрд░рд╡рд╕реЗ) рд╡рд╛ рдпрд╢ рд╕реБрдирд╛ рдЧрдпрд╛ рдЬрд┐рд╕рдХрд╛ рдЙрд╕рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдорд╣рд┐) рдмреЬреЗ (рдиреГрдореНрдгрдореН) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдЕрднреНрдпрд╛рд╕ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рдЬрд┐рд╕рдХрд╛, рдЙрд╕рдХрд╛ (рдЖ, рдЕрд░реНрдЪрдд) рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░реЛ реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛ ! рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧ рд╕рджрд╛ рд╣реА рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд░рд╣рд┐рдд рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛрдВ рдХреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдХреЗ рджрд╛рди рд╕реЗ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╡рд╛рдиреН рдХрд░реЛ, рд╕рддреНрдп рдФрд░ рдЕрд╕рддреНрдп рдХрд╛ рд╡рд┐рдЪрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рдХреЗ рд╕рддреНрдп рдХрд╛ рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХрд░рд╛рдп рдХреЗ рдЕрд╕рддреНрдп рдХрд╛ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧ рдХрд░рд╛рдЗрдпреЗ рдФрд░ рд╕рдм рдХреЗ рд╕реБрдЦ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдп рдХреЛ рдЗрдХрдЯреНрдард╛ рдХрд░реЛ реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рджрд┐рд╡реЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ ! рдпреВрдпрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рдирд╡реЗ рдорд╛рд░реБрддрд╛рдп рд╢рд░реНрдзрд╛рдпреЗрдорд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдирдЬ рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрдЪреНрдпреБрддреЗ рдШрд░реНрдорд╕реНрддреБрднреЗ рдкреГрд╖реНрдардпрдЬреНрд╡рдиреЗ рджреНрдпреБрдореНрдирд╢реНрд░рд╡рд╕реЗ рдорд╣рд┐ рдиреГрдореНрдгрдорд╛рд░реНрдЪрдд реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрдердВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рдГ рдХрдердВ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдкреНрд░) (рд╢рд░реНрдзрд╛рдп) рдмрд▓рд╛рдп (рдорд╛рд░реБрддрд╛рдп) рдорд░реБрддрд╛рдорд┐рджрдВ рддрд╕реНрдореИ (рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рдирд╡реЗ) рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпрд╛ рднрд╛рдирд╡реЛ рджреАрдкреНрддрдпреЛ рдпрд╕реНрдп рддрд╕реНрдореИ (рдЗрдорд╛рдореН) рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдореН (рд╡рд╛рдЪрдореН) рд╕реБрд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛рдгреАрдореН (рдЕрдирдЬ) рдЙрдЪреНрдЪрд░рддреЛрдкрджрд┐рд╢рддред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕рдВрд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдпрд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГ, рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрдиреИрдХрд╡рдЪрдирдВ рдЪред (рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрдЪреНрдпреБрддреЗ) рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрд╛рдиреНрдореЗрдШрд╛рдЪреНрдЪреНрдпреБрддреЛ рдпрдГ рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрдВ рдореЗрдШрдВ рдЪреНрдпрд╛рд╡рдпрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛ рддрд╕реНрдореИ (рдШрд░реНрдорд╕реНрддреБрднреЗ) рдпреЛ рдШрд░реНрдордВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдВ рд╕реНрддреЛрднрддрд┐ рд╕реНрддреМрддрд┐ рддрд╕реНрдореИ (рджрд┐рд╡рдГ) рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ (рдЖ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН (рдкреГрд╖реНрдардпрдЬреНрд╡рдиреЗ) рдпрдГ рдкреГрд╖реНрдареЗрди рдпрдЬрддрд┐ рддрд╕реНрдореИ (рджреНрдпреБрдореНрдирд╢реНрд░рд╡рд╕реЗ) рджреНрдпреБрдореНрдирдВ рдпрд╢рдГ рд╢реНрд░рд╡рдГ рд╢реНрд░реБрддрдВ рдпрд╕реНрдп рддрд╕реНрдореИ (рдорд╣рд┐) рдорд╣рддреН (рдиреГрдореНрдгрдореН) рдирд░реЛрд╜рднреНрдпрд╕реНрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдпрддреНрддрддреН (рдЕрд░реНрдЪрдд) рд╕рддреНрдХреБрд░реБрдд реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ ! рдпреВрдпрдВ рд╕рджреИрд╡рд╛рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рджрд╛рдиреЗрди рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╡рддрдГ рдХреБрд░реБрдд рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рд╕рддреНрдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдЪреНрдп рд╕рддреНрдпрдВ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╣рдпрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рд╜рд╕рддреНрдпрдВ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЬрдпрдд рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдпреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдВ рд╕рдЮреНрдЪрд┐рдиреБрдд реерезрее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдпрд╛ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рдд рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрдд рд╡ рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдЪреЗ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдЕрд╕рд▓реНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рдпрд╛ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рдЪреА рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдмрд░реЛрдмрд░ рд╕рдВрдЧрддреА рдЬрд╛рдгрд╛рд╡реА.

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрдиреЛ! рддреБрдореНрд╣реА рд╕рджреИрд╡ рдЕрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдиреА рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдВрдирд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рджрд╛рди рдХрд░рд╛ рд╡ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирджрд╛рди рдХрд░рд╛. рд╕рддреНрдп-рдЕрд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдЪрд╛ рд╡рд┐рдЪрд╛рд░ рдХрд░реВрди рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдЪрд╛ рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рд╡рд╛ рд╡ рдЕрд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдЪрд╛ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧ рдХрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛ рдЖрдгрд┐ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдЪреНрдпрд╛ рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рд╕рд╛рдареА рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рд╕рдВрдкрд╛рджрд┐рдд рдХрд░рд╛. рее рез рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYour (cohort), Maruts, is conspicous, mighty shedding water and augmenting food; yoking your horse (to your cars), spreading everywhere, and combined with the lightning, the triple-stationed company roars aloud, and the circumambient waters fall upon the earth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Forth, o Maruts, (go) your forceful, water-seeking, vigor-increasing, horse-yoked, swirling (chariots?).
They join with lightning; Trita [/the third (heaven)] bellows. The waters resound, swirling in their streambed.

Jamison Brereton Notes

p├бrijrayaс╕е seems almost like a univerbation of a prepositional/adverbial phrase p├бri *jr├бyaс╕е тАЬaround the (broad) expanse.тАЭ It is even possible that one of the forms in this vs. is meant to represent the adverbial phrase – so, possibly, ab тАЬforth (go your chariots) around the expanse,тАЭ referring to the MarutsтАЩ circling the earth or the midspace – while the other is a nom. pl. (by old haplology), to be rendered as in the published translation: тАЬthe waters swirling in their stream bed.тАЭ This would alleviate the clunkiness of the repetition, which would then be only apparent. As Geldner remarks (n. 2c), тАЬTrita’s Beziehung zu den Marut ist dunkel.тАЭ Trita is associated with the Maruts also in II.34.10, 14. In vs. 10 of that hymn Trita seems to be associated with making noise, as here; that is as far as I can get.

Griffith

O Maruts, rich in water, strengtheners of life are your strong bands with harnessed steeds, that wander far.
Trita roars out at him who aims the lightning-flash. The waters sweeping round are thundering on their way.

Geldner

Es sollen eure starken, Wasser holenden, kraftreichen, rossebespannten Wagen in ihrem Wettlauf zum Vorschein kommen, ihr Marut. Sie legen Blitze als Pfeile auf; Trita br├╝llt, die Wasser rauschen, in dem Flu├Яbett ihren Wettlauf machend.

Grassmann

Euch vor, o Maruts, ziehn die feuchten Reisigen, euch Rosse schirrend, m├дchtig, die erfrischenden; Mit Blitz beschenkt euch Trita, br├╝llt mit Donnerton, die Wasser rauschen, reisend rings auf ihrer Bahn.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe Maruts (appear) radiant with lightning, leaders (of the rain), armed with weapons of adamant, blazing with the wind, the precipitators of mountains, the repeated distributors of water, wielders of the thunderbolt, roaring in concert, combining (to send rain), and of exceeding strength.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

With lightning as their might and stones as their missiles, the superior men, the Maruts, turbulent as the wind, shaking the mountains, (though) just with a desire to give water, roll hailstones in an instantтАФ (they) with thundering onslaught, violent, overpowering.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda-final parvatacy├║t- returns here (from 1b) but in a different form: nom. pl. -aс╕е rather than dat. sg. -e.

Griffith

They gleam with lightning, Heroes, Casters of the Stone, wind-rapid Maruts, overthrowers of the bills,
Oft through desire to rain coming with storm of hail, roaring in onset, violent and exceeding strong.

Geldner

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPowerful Rudras, you urge on the nights and days the firmament and the worlds; agitators (of all things), you toss the clouds like ships (in the sea), so (you throw down) the strong plural ces (of the enemy); but, Maruts you do no harm.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Through the nights, o Rudras, through the days, you skillful ones, through the midspace, through the dusky realms, you shakers,
through the fields when you drive, like boats (through the water)тАФ through (all these places) of difficult going, o Maruts, you never suffer harm.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The vs. sets up pairs of antitheses: nights/days (a), midspace/dusky realms (b), with the third only indirectly implied: fields [=dry land]/ *water [via boats] (c).

The ─лm that interrupts the simile n─Б╠Бvaс╕е тАж yath─Б in c is superficially puzzling, but I think it is related to the implication just noted: it stands for the acc. тАШwatersтАЩ in the full realization of the phrase тАЬlike boats (through waters).тАЭ It is also worthy of note that the cadences of p─Бdas c and d are phonologically similar, esp. at beginning and end, though they achieve this through very different grammatical means: тАж n─Б╠Бva ─лс╣Г yath─Б # тАж n─Б╠Бha riс╣гyatha #.

Griffith

When, mighty Rudras, through the nights and through the days, when through the sky and realms of air, shakers of all,
When over the broad fields ye drive along like ships, e’en to strongholds ye come, Maruts, but are not harmed.

Geldner

Ihr durchfahret die N├дchte, die Tage, ihr Rudras├╢hne, ihr Ge├╝bten, die Luft, die R├дume, ihr Sch├╝ttler. Wenn ihr die Ebenen durchfahret wie Schiffe das Wasser und die unwegsamen Gegenden, ihr Marut, so nehmet ihr niemals Schaden.

Grassmann

Wenn, m├дcht’ge Rudra’s, N├дchte, wenn die Tage ihr, wenn ihr die Luft durchdringt, Ersch├╝ttrer, und den Raum; Wenn ihr durch Fluren fahret wie auf einem Schiff, wenn durch die Wildniss, trifft euch Maruts Schaden nie.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYour prowess, Maruts, has spread wide your glory as the sun (sends afar his) radiance, or the white (horses of the gods travel far) in their course; of unbounded lustre, you close the cloud withholding the waters.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This is your heroism, your greatness, o Maruts: it stretches across a long wagon-trek [=measure of distance], like the sun.
(You are) like antelopes on your journey, with ungraspable brilliance, when you have overrun the mountain that does not give horses
[/gives non-horses (=cows?)].

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the phonetic echoes: (mahi)t(v)an├б(m) тАж (ta)t─Бna тАж (├й)t─Б n├б тАж (├бy─Б)tan─Б.

I take тАЬgreatnessтАЭ (or тАЬheroism [and] greatnessтАЭ) to be the unexpressed subj.

of tat─Бna in b, rather than y├│janam with Geldner The latter is an acc. of extent of space, and the phrase #d─лrgh├бm тАж y├│janam# is iconically positioned to express the distance traversed.

In the second hemistich contra Geldner and Renou I take c as a separate nominal main clause, with d a temporal dependent cl. This allows the y├бd to be properly positioned, rather than occurring deep in the dependent cl. (The Witzel Got┼Н treatment is similar to mine.) The shared characteristic in the simile in c, тАШhaving ungraspable brillianceтАЩ (├бgс╣Ыbh─лta┼Ыocis-), presumably refers to the combination of speed and timidity that characterizes antelopes, deer, and their ilk and makes them hard to catch. If we were to speculate more narrowly, the тАШbrillianceтАЩ might refer either to the conspicuous white spots on the coat of the chital deer or the white sides, underbelly, interior legs, and hindquarters of the blackbuck – both species that seem native to the right location.

The puzzle in d is the phrase ├бna┼Ыvad─Бm тАж gir├нm тАЬthe non-horse-giving mountain.тАЭ In order to approach it, we might first tackle the verb that governs it, ny ├бy─Бtan─Б. The lexeme n├н тИЪy─Б is generally hostile; cf. nearby V.42.10 (also of the Maruts) y├б ├│hate rakс╣г├бso dev├бv─лt─Бv / acakr├йbhis t├бm maruto n├н y─Бta тАЬWho(ever) will laud the demons at the invitation to the gods, run him over/down, Maruts, with your wheel-less (chariots).тАЭ In our passage the sense seems to be that the Maruts trample down or overrun a mountain whose behavior deserves it. But what is a non-horsegiving mountain? On the one hand, it may simply refer to a stingy mountain, comparable to a stingy patron, contrasted to a┼Ыvad─Б╠Б- тАШhorse-givingтАЩ used of generous patrons elsewhere. But still, why horses? Mountains can be the source of nourishment and wealth; cf. I.65.5 g├нrir n├б bh├║jma тАЬa source of benefit like a mountainтАЭ (also VIII.50.2 and comm. ad I.55.3). But mountainous terrain is not particularly friendly to horses, which are most at home in open, relatively flat grasslands. I therefore wonder if the operable segmentation of the cmpd is ana┼Ыvad─Б╠Б- тАШgiving non-horsesтАЩ (rather than an-a┼Ыvad─Б- тАШnot giving horsesтАЩ). This might then be an oblique reference to the Vala myth and the mountain that yields up cows (that is, non-horses). However, since the Maruts are not generally associated with the Vala myth, this may be farfetched. The safest interpr. is OldenbergтАЩs deflection, that the phrase is тАЬauf unbekannte Erz├дhlung anspielend.тАЭ

Griffith

Maruts, this hero strength and majesty of yours hath, like the Sun, extended o’er a lengthened way,
When in your course like deer with splendour unsubdued ye bowed the hill that gives imperishable rain.

Dies ist eure St├дrke, eure Gr├╢├Яe, ihr Marut: Eure lange Wegstrecke hat sich ausgedehnt wie die der Sonne, als ihr von nicht zu nehmendem Feuerglanz, schnell wie die Antilopen im Laufe in den Berg hineinfuhret, der die Rosse nicht herausgab.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, dispensers of rain, your strength is manifested when, shaking the water-laden cloud, you let loose the shower; conjointly propitiated, conduct us by an easy path leading to prosperity, as the eye (shows the way).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When the heaving troop has flashed, o Maruts, you will plunder the tree like a caterpillar, you (ritual) adepts.
Then in concert you will lead Proper Thinking [/Aramati] to us along an easy way, like the eye (of the sun? of the traveler himself?)
(leading) the traveler.

Jamison Brereton Notes

My interpr. follows that of Narten (Sig.Aor. 195-96), with the first p─Бda consisting of the y├бd clause, the 2nd the main cl. Both Geldner and Renou take the first part of p─Бda a as the main cl., with the dependent clause starting with y├бd. Although y├бd is better positioned in their interpr. than in NartenтАЩs, they must make arс╣Зas├бm an obj.

of m├│с╣гath─Б (in unconvincing fashion) and the sequence of tense/mood is badly off: aug. aor. ├бbhr─Бji тАж aor. subjunctive m├│с╣гath─Б, lit., тАЬit has flashed when you will steal тАжтАЭ Geldner simply renders the subjunctive as a preterite, while RenouтАЩs parenthesis in тАЬvous d├йrob(i)ezтАЭ is masterfully evasive even for him.

As I just said, I am not happy with the position of y├бd in NartenтАЩs/my interpr., since it follows both the verb and part of the subject (plus a voc., but that doesnтАЩt count). There is another possibility, that y├бd functions here as a sort of izafe, connecting ┼Ы├бrdhaс╕е and arс╣Зas├бm: тАЬthe troop, which is a flood.тАЭ In this case ├бbhr─Бji would be a main-cl. verb, and the two p─Бdas, a and b, would be syntactically unconnected: тАЬThe troop that is a flood has flashed; you will plunder тАжтАЭ arс╣Зas├б- is a hapax. Narten takes it as an adjectival deriv. of ├бrс╣Зas- тАШfloodтАЩ, but it could have been (re-)substantivized as тАШfloodтАЩ.

The point of comparison in b between the Maruts and the caterpillar is that violent storms also strip the leaves off trees.

The sequence vс╣Ыkс╣г├бс╣Г kap(an├йva) is oddly reminiscent of Vс╣Ыс╣г─Бkapi, the randy monkey in X.86, but this must be accidental.

In the published translation the voc. sajoс╣гasaс╕е is not rendered as a voc., since the Engl.

would be awkward.

The s-aor. subj. neс╣гath─Б тАШyou will leadтАЩ is particularly appropriate to the obj.

ar├бmati-, the personified feminine Proper Thinking, since the verb тИЪn─л, esp. in sigmatic forms, becomes specialized for leading females in ritual settings; cf. the priestly title Neс╣гс╣нar. Although n├йс╣гс╣нar- probably owes its -с╣г- to crossing of the agent noun n├йtar- with Tvaс╣гс╣нar (tv├бс╣гс╣нar-), who is also associated with ritual females (see EWA s.v. n├йс╣гс╣нar-), its apparent coincidence with the neс╣г of the s-aor. could spread the semantics.

Griffith

Bright shone your host, ye Sages, Maruts, when ye smote the waving tree as when the worm consumeth it.
Accordant, as the eye guides him who walks, have ye led our devotion onward by an easy path.

Eure Heerschar, ihr Marut, ergl├дnzte, als ihr das Rindermeer beraubtet wie die Raupe den Baum, ihr Meister. Nun m├╢get ihr Eintr├дchtigen, unsere Andacht auf den guten Weg f├╝hren wie das Auge den Gehenden.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe sage, or the sovereign, whom you, Maruts, direct, is never overcome nor slain; he perishes not, nor suffers pain, nor undergoes injury, nor are his riches or his safety imperilled.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He is not conquered, o Maruts, nor is he slain, nor does he fail, nor waver, nor suffer harm,
nor do his riches give out, nor his helpтАФthe seer or the king whom you will тАЬsweeten.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

In d the sequence с╣Ы╠Бс╣гiс╣Г v─Б must have been fronted around the rel. y├бm, since the phrase as a whole с╣Ы╠Бс╣гiс╣Г v─Б y├бс╣Г r─Б╠Бj─Бnaс╣Г v─Б does not mean тАЬeither the seer or which kingтАЭ but тАЬwhich seer or kingтАЭ – or even better тАЬwhich one, whether seer or king.тАЭ I take the thematic stem s├║с╣г┼лda- as ultimately deriving from a pf. subjunctive, despite accent. In this particular form, the 2nd pl. indic. pf. *s├║с╣г┼лda, with the rarely occuring 2nd pl. act. pf. ending -a, would have simply been extended by the prim.

ending.

Griffith

Never is he, O Maruts, slain or overcome, never doth he decay ne’er is distressed or harmed;
His treasures, his resources, never waste away, whom. whether he be prince or Rsi, ye direct.

Geldner

Der wird nicht vergewaltigt noch erschlagen, ihr Marut, der erleidet keinen Unfall, verliert nicht den Halt, kommt nicht zu Schaden, nicht versiegen seine Reicht├╝mer und Hilfen, den ihr - sei er Rishi oder K├╢nig - zum Meister macht.

Grassmann

Nicht wird besiegt, o Maruts, nicht geschlagen der, den ihr begl├╝ckt, sei Dichter oder K├╢nig er; Nicht geht er fehl, nicht wankt er, nicht wird er verletzt, nicht schwindet hin sein Reichthum, seine H├╝lfen nicht.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLords of the Niyut steeds, overcomers of multitudes leaders (of rites), radiant as the ─Аdityas, are the dispensers of water; when sovereign lords, they fill the clouds, and, loud sounding, moisten the earth with sweet (watery) sustenance.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The Maruts have teams (of horses) like men who conquer in roving bands; they have (water) skins [=clouds] like hospitable
(householders):
they swell the wellspring. When the strong ones have sounded, they inundate the earth with the stalk of honey.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In the cmpd. gr─Бmaj├нt- the 1st member could have either an acc. or an instr.

relationship with the root noun. Both would be possible: тАШconquering roving bandтАЩ (so Grassmann, Geldner, Renou, Thieme [M+A 81]) or тАШconquering with/in roving bandsтАЩ. Although in such root noun cmpds an acc. relationship is more common, indeed also among cmpds in -j├нt-, I follow ScarlattaтАЩs preferred interpr. (156) found also in his tr. (=Witzel Got┼Н), although the acc. interpr. is hardly excluded. The parallel I.100.10 gr─Б╠Бmebhiс╕е s├бnit─Б, cited by Renou, is suggestive.

My interpr. of b follows Thieme (M+A 81), esp. of aryam├бс╣Зaс╕е, which he takes as тАЬhospitable ones (hospitable householders who refresh the stranger).тАЭ Others take it as a pregnant pl. referring to тАЬ(Mitra, Varuс╣Зa, and) Aryaman.тАЭ The dep. cl. in c, y├бd in─Б╠Бso ├бsvaran, can be construed either with what precedes or what follows, but sits uneasily with either because of its augmented ├бsvaran, which doesnтАЩt match the pres. indic. p├нnvanti (c) or undanti (d). I chose to connect it with d, as thunder before rain.

Griffith

With harnessed team like heroes overcoming troops, the friendly Maruts, laden with their water-casks,
Let the spring flow, and when impetuous’ they roar they inundate the earth with floods of pleasant meath.

Geldner

Mit Geschenken versehen wie M├дnner, die einen Clan besiegen, wie die G├╢nner, lassen die Schlauchtr├дger Marut den Brunnen ├╝berquellen, wenn die Gewaltigen brausen. Sie durchnetzen die Erde mit dem Trank des Metes.

Grassmann

Reich an Gespannen, Heerbesiegern, Helden gleich, wie Busenfreunde f├╝llen sie die Quelle an, Die starken Maruts, Tonnen f├╝hrend, rauschen hell, die Erde netzen rings sie mit des Honigs Seim.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis wide-extended earth is for the Maruts; the spacious heaven is for the spreading winds; the paths of the firmament are provided (for their course); for them the expanding clouds quickly bestow (their gifts).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

This wide-extended earth: pravatvat─л pс╣Ыthiv─л: pra-vat, having extent, extension;

Vat = again, having or possessing;

Pravatvat = extensive; or, may imply having pre-eminence; or, tat-para, being subject to it, as the earth is subject to the Maruts, or they pervade the whole earth, kс╣Ыtsnam bh┼лmim vy─Бpnuvant; so the heaven is pravatvat─л, spacious or subject to the pravats, pravatbhyaс╕е the pre-eminent of spreading Maruts

Jamison Brereton

This earth slopes gently for the Maruts; heaven becomes gently sloping for them when they go forth;
the paths of the midspace slope gently; gently slope the mountains of lively drops.

Jamison Brereton Notes

dya├║с╕е is clearly fem. here, given the adj. prav├бtvat─л, but this gender choice must be conditioned by its standard formulaic partner, fem. pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Б, in the preceding p─Бda, modified by the same adj. in the same position.

The nom. pl. j─лr├бd─Бnavaс╕е тАШhaving lively dropsтАЩ in d must modify the mountains (p├бrvat─Бс╕е), but in the immed. preceding hymn it is found in the voc. of the Maruts (V.53.6, in the same metrical pos.; cf. also I.34.4 a nom. pl. of the Maruts in the same position). There are no grounds for emending the text by deleting the accent and making it into a voc. (which would also entail a switch from 3rd to 2nd ps. ref.); how would it have acquired the accent here? Rather it must be word play: mountains produce torrents of water when it rains.

Griffith

Free for the Maruts is the earth with sloping ways, free for the rushing Ones is heaven with steep descents.
The paths of air’s mid-region are precipitous, precipitous the mountains with their running streams.

Geldner

Gebahnt ist f├╝r die ausziehenden Marut diese Erde, gebahnt der Himmel, gebahnt die Wege durch die Luft, gebahnt die Berge , die schnelle Gabe gew├дhren.

Grassmann

Leichtgangbar ist die Erde hier der Marutschar, leichtgangbar auch der Himmel dort den schreitenden; Leichtgangbar sind die Pfade durch der L├╝fte Raum, leichtgangbar auch die quellenreichen Bergesh├╢hn.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рд╣реЗ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рд╕рднрд░рд╕рдГ рд╕рд╣рдмрд▓рд╛рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдгрд░рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдиреЗрддрд╛рд░реЛ рдпреВрдпрдВ рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреЗ рдЙрджрд┐рддреЗ рдЙрджреНрдЧрддреЗ рдордзреНрдпрд╛рд╣реНрдиреЗ рдорджрде рд╕реЛрдореЗрди рд╣реЗ рджрд┐рд╡рдГ рджреНрдпреБрд▓реЛрдХрд╕реНрдп рдирд░рдГ рдиреЗрддрд╛рд░рдГ ред рдпрджрд╛ рд╕реЛрдордВ рдкрд╛рддреБрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдереЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рддрджрд╛ рд╡реЛрд╜рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╕рд┐рд╕реНрд░рддрдГ рд╕рд░рдиреНрддрдГ рди рдЕрд╣ рд╢реНрд░рдердпрдиреНрдд рдиреИрд╡ рд╢реНрд▓рдердпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╕рджреНрдпрдГ рддрджрд╛рдиреАрдореЗрд╡ рдЕрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдзреНрд╡рдирдГ рджреЗрд╡рдпрдЬрдирдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╕реНрдп рдкрд╛рд░рдорд╢реНрдиреБрде рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдиреБрде ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдпрджрд╛ рд╕реЛрдореЗрди рдорджрде рддрджрд╛ рддреНрд╡рджреАрдпрд╛ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛ рди рд╢рд┐рдерд┐рд▓рд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдпреВрдпрдВ рдЪ рдХреГрддреНрд╕реНрдирд╕реНрдп рд▓реЛрдХрддреНрд░рдпрдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╕реНрдп рдкрд╛рд░рдорд╢реНрдиреБрде рее рее резрел рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaruts of combined strength, leaders of the universe, guides of heaven, when the sun has risen you rejoice (in the Soma beverage), then your rapid steeds know no relaxation, but quickly you reach the limits of this road (to the sacrifice).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Leaders of the universe: svarс╣Зaraс╕е = sarvasya net─Бraс╕е, leaders of all; divo naraс╕е = leaders of heaven

Jamison Brereton

WhileтАФyou Maruts of equal gravity, you sunlike men, you men of heavenтАФyou become exhilarated when the sun has risen,
your horses certainly never slacken as they run. In a single day you reach the far limit of this road.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The s-stem adj. s├б-bharas- (so accented in X.101.3, though it is an accentless voc. here), tr. here тАШof equal gravityтАЩ, is a bahuvr─лhi with the lit. sense тАШhaving the same burden / weightтАЩ, with the same -bharas- as in vi┼Ыv├б-bharas- тАШbringing allтАЩ, i.e., lit. тАШhaving/bringing all burdensтАЩ in IV.1.19.

s u varс╣Зaraс╕е at the end of p─Бda a picks up n├бraс╕е at the end of 8a and 10b and asvaran at the end of 8c.

Griffith

When, as the Sun hath risen up, ye take delight, O bounteous radiant Maruts, Heroes of the sky,
Your coursers weary not when speeding on.their way, and rapidly ye reach the end of this your path.

Geldner

Wenn ihr gleichgewichtigen Marut, ihr Sonnenm├дnner, ihr Mannen des Himmels bei Sonnenaufgang ausgelassen seid, so lassen eure Rosse in ihrem Laufe niemals locker. An einem Tage erreichet ihr das Ende dieses Weges.

Grassmann

Wenn ihr, o Maruts, gabenreiche Glanzesherrn, bei Sonnenaufgang, Himmelsm├дnner, euch berauscht, Dann suchen nimmer eure schnellen Rosse Rast, in einem Tag erreicht ihr dieses Weges Ziel.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLances (gleam), Maruts, upon your shoulders, anklets on your feet, golden cuirasses on your breasts, and pure (waters shine) in your chariots; lightning blazing with fire in your hands, and golden tiarsa are towering on your heads.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

┼Ъipr─Бс╕е ┼Ыirс╣гasu vitat─Б hiraс╣Зyay─лс╕е: ┼Ыipra = uс╣гс╣З─лс╣гamayaс╕е, composed of turbans or head-dresses

Jamison Brereton

On your shoulders spears, on your feet spangles; on your breasts brilliants, o Maruts, on your chariot charms.
Lightning bolts with the flash of fire in your fists, golden (helmet-)lips stretched out on your heads.

Griffith

Lances are on your shoulders, anklets on your feet, gold chains are on your breasts, gems, Maruts, on your car.
Lightnings aglow with flame are flashing in your hands, and visors wroughtof gold are laid upon your heads.

Geldner

Auf euren Schultern sind die Speere, an den F├╝├Яen die Spangen, an der Brust die Goldm├╝nzen, ihr Marut, am Wagen die Prunkst├╝cke, feuergl├дnzende Blitze in euren H├дnden, an den H├дuptern dehnen sich die goldenen Zahnreihen aus.

Grassmann

Auf euren Schultern Lanzen, Spangen an dem Fuss, Geschmeid’ am Busen, Maruts, und am Wagen Schmuck, In euren Armen Blitze wie die Flammen hell, an euren H├дuptern breiten goldne Helme sich.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, when moving, you agitate the heaven of unchecked radiance, and (stir) the bright water; when you combine your energies and are shining brilliantly, and when purposing to send down rain, you utter a loud shout.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

And stir the bright water: the text changes the person n of the verb, yat svaranti ghoс╣гam, when they sound a noise; i.e. when the Maruts make a fearful noise, or when the worshippers utter loud praises

Jamison Brereton

The vault whose brilliance is ungraspable for the stranger do you, Maruts, shake for the gleaming fig [=rain].
The communities huddle together when (the Maruts) have grown
turbulent. The truth seekers sound an extended cry.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the repetition of ├бgс╣Ыbh─лta-┼Ыociс╣г- from 5c; this cmpd is found only once elsewhere in the RV (VIII.23.1, of Agni).

The first hemistich is discussed in some detail by Thieme (Fremd. 68-70), whose interpr. I basically follow. I would add that the (heavenly) brilliance that cannot be grasped by the ─Аrya on earth is shaken down as rain by the Maruts.

There are two basic interpr. of c, depending on what the subject of s├бm acyanta is taken to be. For Geldner the subj. is the Maruts, with vс╣Ыj├бn─Б the grammatical obj. referring to their girthbands: they are girding themselves for battle. Witzel Got┼НтАЩs interpr. also takes the reference to be to the Maruts, but with vс╣Ыj├бn─Б as the subj. referring to the closing of the ranks (Reihe) of the Maruts, again before some warlike manoeuvre on their part. In both these interpr. the referent of the subj. of s├бm acyanta and ├бtitviс╣гanta is the same: the Maruts. With Renou I instead consider the verbs to have different subjects: the subj. of s├бm acyanta, vс╣Ыj├бn─Б, refers to the circles or communities of the ─Аrya, while the Maruts are the subj. of ├бtitviс╣гanta. I think the two hemistichs contrast the MarutsтАЩ effects on the ─Аrya communities: in ab the Maruts bring them the welcome rain they cannot get themselves, but in cd they cling together during the violence of the MarutsтАЩ storm. (I cannot decide which strain K├╝mmelтАЩs tr. (224) follows, though Witzel Got┼НтАЩs paraphrase of it in their n. leans towards the Renou/JB side.)

Griffith

Maruts, in eager stir ye shake the vault of heaven, splendid beyond conception, for its shining fruit.
They gathered when they let their deeds of might flash forth. The Pious Ones send forth a far-resounding shout.

Geldner

Vom Himmel, der sich seinen Feuerglanz nicht von dem Vornehmen nehmen l├д├Яt, sch├╝ttelt ihr Marut die hellfarbige Beere. Sie ziehen ihre G├╝rtel zu, wenn sie in Feuer geraten sind, sie stimmen ihr weitgedehntes Get├╢se an, den rechten Weg liebend.

Grassmann

Ihr Maruts sch├╝ttelt eifrig von dem Himmel ab, dem unerreichbar gl├дnzenden die helle Frucht, Zusammen st├╝rzen Schluchten, wenn erregt ihr seid, wenn ihr, die heil’gen, weithin sendet eur Get├╢n.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay we, who are possessed of chariots, intelligent Maruts, become (proprietors) of wealth, comprising food bestowed by you; of wealth that vanishes not, as Tiс╣гya (declines not) from the sky; therefore, Maruts, gratify us with infinite (riches).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Tiс╣гya: = ─Аditya; it is the eighth lunar mansion

Jamison Brereton

May we be the charioteers of the vigorous wealth given by you, discriminating Maruts,
which does not stay away (from us), any more than Tiс╣гya [=Dog Star] from heaven. By us enjoy (wealth) in thousands, Maruts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The verb in d, r─Бranta, presents difficulties both morphologically and semantically. Formally it has received a variety of analyses: Grassmann classifies it (impossibly) with тИЪradh тАШsubdueтАЩ; as Oldenberg notes, in context it would best belong to тИЪr─Б тАШgiveтАЩ, but it is hard to make this work formally. Given the long redupl.

characteristic of the pf. to тИЪran тАШenjoyтАЩ, the form most likely belongs there. Lubotsky

classifies it as a med. (3rd sg.) injunc. to that root, but there are no other med. forms to this stem or indeed to the root (raс╣З├бyanta being an -anta replacement). I think we are therefore stuck with the formally most likely analysis, given by K├╝mmel, as 2nd pl. pf.

impv., with (as often) irregular full grade (see also Geldner n. 13d). This poses problems semantically. It should mean тАШenjoyтАЩ, with the Maruts as subject. The gapped obj. is qualified by sahasr├нn- тАШpossessing/in thousandsтАЩ; as Renou points out, this is a stable epithet of ray├н- тАШwealthтАЩ. And this is the problem: the Maruts have just given us wealth; we should be the ones enjoying it. Gods never enjoy wealth – they distribute it. Geldner suggests in his n. that the thousandfold wealth they enjoy is тАЬin Gestalt von Opfern,тАЭ which is certainly a good try (probably the best available). Oldenberg tries to make the verb into what looks like a reflexive causative: тАЬmacht [den Reichtum] bei uns sich erfreuenтАЭ – that is, the Maruts should make the wealth be happy to stay by us. Witzel Got┼Н go one step further in the causativization process: тАЬ(An diesem Reichtum) тАж macht, dass man sich hier bei uns daran freue тАж am tausendfachen.тАЭ But these last two attempts to separate the Maruts from the enjoyment are unconvincing, because no other forms to this stem show this causative tendency. I think we must stick with the meaning imposed by parallel forms (so also Renou) and deal, perhaps as Geldner does, with the Maruts enjoying riches.

Griffith

Sage Maruts, may we be the drivers of the car of riches ful I of life that have been given by you.
O Maruts, let that wealth in thousands dwell with us which never vanishes like Tisya from the sky.

Geldner

Ihr klugen Marut, wir m├╢chten Lenker des von euch geschenkten lebenskr├дftigen Reichtums sein, der nicht von uns weicht, so wenig wie Tisya vom Himmel. Bei uns freuet euch an dem tausendfachen Reichtum, ihr Marut!

Grassmann

O weise Maruts, lasst uns Wagenlenker sein des labungsreichen uns von euch geschenkten Guts, Das nicht sich fern h├дlt wie des Himmels Glanzgestirn; o Maruts gebt uns tausend G├╝ter in die Hand.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou bestow, Maruts, wealth and enviable posterity; you protect the sage learned in the S─Бma; you grant horses and food to (me) the ministrant priest; you render a prince prosperous.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The sage learned in the S─Бma: s─Бmavipram = samn─Бm vividh─Бm prerayit─Бram, the prompt or instrumental gator, in various ways, of the S─Бma hymns

Jamison Brereton

You, Maruts, (aid) our wealth consisting of coveted heroes; you aid the seer inspired in his melody.
You (establish) a charger and a prize for Bharata; you establish a king with attentive hearing.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The problematic wealth of 13d reappears in 14a as the obj. of a gapped verb whose subj. is the Maruts, but in this case we can borrow the verb from the next p─Бda, avatha тАШyou aidтАЩ. Geldner unaccountably supplies a verb (тАЬgew├дhretтАЭ) that matches neither what precedes nor what follows.

The p─Бda-final words in the first hemistich, тАж sp─Бrh├бv─лram# and тАж s─Б╠Бmavipram# are phonologically similar. This partial match may help explain the odd hapax s─Б╠Бmavipra-. Although my tr. тАШinspired in his melodyтАЩ is structurally similar to the other standard renderings (e.g., Renou тАШinspir├й par la m├йlodie-sacre├йтАЩ), the cmpd should not mean that. For one thing the 2nd member v├нpra- is almost never used adjectivally (pace Grassmann), but almost always as a noun referring to a type of poet.

Moreover, the accent strong suggests a bahuvr─лhi. A literal rendering of such a bahuvr─лhi would be something like тАШwhose inspired poet is the melodyтАЩ or тАШwhose inspired poet has the melodyтАЩ (latter like v├бjra-b─Бhu- тАШhaving an arm that has a mace (in it)тАЩ), which do not work as descriptors of a seer. I wonder if the phonological play just noted didnтАЩt flip the order of the cmpd members, and the underlying form would be *v├нpra-s─Бman- тАШhaving the melody of an inspired poetтАЩ. Exact parallels are v├нpramanman- тАШhaving the thought of an inspired poet / having inspired thoughtтАЩ in VI.39.1, where it modifies kav├н-, and v├нpra-vacas- тАШhaving the speech of an inspired poet / having inspired speechтАЩ in VIII.61.8.

English translation:

тАЬTherefore do I solicit wealth of you, who are prompt to grant protection, whereby we may multiply our descendants, as the sun (spreads wide his rays); be propitiated, Maruts, by this my praise, by the efficacy whereof may we pass over a hundred winters.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For this treasure I beseech you, you of immediate aid, by which we will extend (our control) over men like the sun.
Take pleasure, Maruts, in this speech of mine, by whose enduring
power may we pass through a hundred winters.

Griffith

Of you, most swift to succour! I solicit wealth wherewith we may spread forth mid men like as the Sun.
Accept, O Maruts, graciously this hymn of mine that we may live a hundred winters through its power.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рддрддреН) (рд╡рдГ) рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рддреН (рдпрд╛рдорд┐) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрдорд┐ (рджреНрд░рд╡рд┐рдгрдореН) рдзрдирдВ рдпрд╢реЛ рд╡рд╛ (рд╕рджреНрдпрдКрддрдпрдГ) рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рджреАрдирд┐ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рддреЗ (рдпреЗрдирд╛) (рд╕реНрд╡рдГ) рд╕реБрдЦрдореН (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рддрддрдирд╛рдо) рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреАрд░реНрдгреАрдпрд╛рдо (рдиреДрдиреН) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреН (рдЕрднрд┐) (рдЗрджрдореН) (рд╕реБ) (рдореЗ) (рдорд░реБрддрдГ) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ (рд╣рд░реНрдпрддрд╛) рдХрд╛рдордпрдзреНрд╡рдореН (рд╡рдЪрдГ) рд╡рдЪрдирдореН (рдпрд╕реНрдп) (рддрд░реЗрдо) (рддрд░рд╕рд╛) рдмрд▓реЗрди (рдирд┐рдШрдВрежреи.реп) (рд╢рддрдореН) (рд╣рд┐рдорд╛рдГ) рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд╛рдгрд┐ реерезрелрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ ! рднрд╡рдиреНрддреЛ рдпрд╢реЛ рдзрдирдВ рд╕реБрдЦрдВ рд╕рддреНрдпрдВ рд╡рдЪреЛ рдмрд▓рдВ рдЪ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдпрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рджреБрдГрдЦрд╛рдирд┐ рддрд░рдиреНрддреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ реерезрелрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрдиреНрд╕реБрдЦрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪрддреБрдГрдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╖реЛрдбрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ
